When we arrived on Aug 19th we were met with the front desk mgr saying ‚Äúdid I tell you that we are short a technician?‚Äù and when did we need the RV back. I informed him that I had not been told they were down a technician when I made the appt & that I needed it by Mon Aug 31st for our Labor Day Trip.

The following day we received a call that the leveling jack in fact needed to be repaired and that one of the other front jacks also needed to be repaired. I was told they were calling around to locate the parts to repair it (they do not do any jack repairs inhouse they send them all out).
On Monday Aug 24th I called to get an update and was told that they had to let go of the technician that had been working on our RV and that the owner & the front desk person had personally gotten under our RV to look at both jacks & that they could not be repaired & had to be replaced.

We decided that we would again do our own investigating & called Bay Hydraulic. They instructed us to bring the jack to them & they would repair. I called Sturken & let them know that we would be in to pick up the rig. When we arrived they handed me a bill for $320 for the inspection. < Review>
I had to get new shoes for my son, who has officially grown out of little kids shoes. I was nervous, and i
on't know her name, but one of the workers was extremely kind and helpful. Without hesitation, she wanted to give my son options by finding all the shoes they had in his size. She was patient with both of us; more than willing to lace up whatever shoes he chose, or help with anything else he wanted. My son has some troubles with speaking and it meant so much to me that she really took the time to listen to him. I would have left 5 stars but I was disappointed with the lady who assisted us with paying. She ignored my son introducing himself. He can be repetitive if he thinks he isn't being heard, and it seemes that it took me speaking up for him before she acknowledged what he was saying. Overall, we had a great experience. If it wasn't for the worker who initially helped us, I don't think we would have had a better experience. Her positive and willing attitude was amazing.< /Review>

<UserId.>117530377774943409912< /UserId.>< user_name>
Nicholas Trullench</user_name>
<date>1623808298026< /date>< rating>
5</rating>
< review>
They have an abundance of items from a plethora of different product categories being sold by an enthusiastic team of friendly people twenty four hours a day.
Really though, this place has a great selection of all the types of products a smokeshop should have.
Lighters and torches galore. Waterpipes of all shapes and sizes at prices that are as low or lower than any other store I've been to. Numerous different designed nails made from titanium, ceramic and quartz.
There's so many kinds of oil burners in every color of the rainbow; some designs I've only encountered here. Most of these are made from Pyrex unless that "unbreakable" glass with that slight amber tone and light pearlescent finish is used - I personally like the latter as they stay smooth longer because of the durability factor.
They have a large inventory of battery powered vaporizers for concentrates and other substances. Multiple color Hunny  Badgers, consumeable accessories like tips and baskets and licensed add-ons such as the Nectar Collector can be found here, all along side the myriad of other products in this ever growing marketspace.
Pricing for everything is very competitive here, even independent amateur jewelers can save on a wide selection of scales that graduate to the tenths, hundredths and even the thousandths place.
All those little nik knacks like silicone containers, dab sticks, butane and everything else you'd expect to see in a smoke shop make an appearance on the shelves here.
The only complaint I might have about this place is that it isn't bigger. There is definitely no empty shelf space in here.
So if you smoke at all; Anything, you will for sure find what you need here. You will find things you didn't know you needed too- that's always nice.
Oh yah, they have cigarettes and tobacco as well. Word.<//review>

<review>Huddart Park is a beautiful park for hike around multiple trails. It is thickly wooded and the trails are well marked.

One can choose trails which are flat or have moderate elevation. There is open space where one can play simple games. There is a sand volley ball court too. And a badminton court. Lots of picnic areas around.

Ample parking across multiple parking lots. Entry fee is $6 per car. Make sure that you carry exact cash if possible, as if the booth is not manned you'll have to drop the fee in a box.

Overall, a fantastic place to spend time with friends and family.< /review></record></dataset><record>

<userid>113515181944940915487<//userid><user_name>Arti Jadhav</user_name><Time>1621310897327</Time><rating>5</rating>< text>
Lonely Trail to Richards Road loop trail is part of Huddart park. Park hours are till 5 pm so parking outside would be a good option, in case you can not get back by 5pm. Park has a big parking lot. Restrooms are available at the trailhead. It‚Äôs around an 8.5 mile moderate hike. We completed it in 4hrs. Trail is shaded, lots of Redwood trees. Keep the trail map handy all the time as there are many diversions, and easy to get off track. There are logs and fallen trees across the trail, be careful while crossing them. Overall nice, quiet hike, good workout. Bonus- enjoy melodious bird chirping while hiking :)<//text>

<rating>4< /rating>< Review>
Beautiful park! It is a little scary driving up as you are competing on the narrow road with cyclists.

Parking is $6 to get in for the day and they will provide you with a map. We thought we knew where our trail started but ended up getting very lost and having to turn back around.

One on the trail, it‚Äôs pretty straight forward. No hidden paths or uncertainties. The markers are short and hard to find from the lot so be sure to ask the ranger about where to start.

All in all this will be a new frequent park to hike to this winter for me.</Review>

<rate>5</rate>< Text>
Nice quiet park. $6 entrance fee per vehicle, but worth it since there's about parking and no worries of looking for a spot. There are several picnic area which can be reserved online, and some drop in picnic areas. Also had 2 sand volleyball courts. Ranger recommended a 5 mile loop (Crystal spring to Dean trail), which is largely shared and passes through lush redwood groves. There's also a shorter 3 mile loop and a liner 10 mile loop that the ranger recommended. Be sure to grab a map as the week meaning sign pays can be quite confusing.<//Text>

<Text>What a beautiful park! First ... logistics: $6 entry fee, no animals. If you qualify for those, this is a place you must visit. The trails are really well upkept and the picnic areas are numerous and diverse. You can picnic on a blanket in the grass or avoid any crowds and relax under the trees at one of the other picnic areas (you could even come here for a weekend hiking date). There is a ton of tree cover here so it's a great place to come on a hot day for either a picnic or moderate difficulty hike. There are a number of shady trails between 1-3 hours depending on how much time you want to spend. I can't wait to come back to this place!<//Text>< pictures>
